The [Floor Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floorgoal) can hold a maximum of four (4) [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).
- Triangle Goal \- A segment of the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) in a corner of the long side of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) closest to the audience. Each < [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal) is bordered by the inside of the [Field Perimeter](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldperimeter) and the inside of the PVC pipe that spans the corner of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field). Each < [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal) has a color, red or blue, determined by its VEX IQ pieces, PVC pipe, and PET sheet. Each < [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal) can hold a maximum of three (3) [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).
- Standoff Goal \- The orange plastic structure mounted to the center of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) with IQ pins or screws.

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/RampGoal.png)

Figure G-1: A [Square Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#squaregoal).

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/FenceGoal.png)

Figure G-2: A < [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal).

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/FloorGoal.png)

Figure G-3: A [Floor Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floorgoal) and [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal).

Load \- The act of legally introducing a [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) or [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) into the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field). See [<SG6>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sg6).

Load Zone \- A red or blue VEX IQ beam that is attached to the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) with VEX IQ pins. The [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone) is intended to receive [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) from a human Loader.

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/LoadingZone.png)

Figure LZ-1: A [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone).

Matching Goal \- A scoring bonus. See [<SC6>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc6).

Placed \- A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) status. See [<SC5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc5).

Preload \- A [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) that is [Loaded](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#load) into a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) prior to a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). See [<SG5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sg5).

Scoring Object \- A plastic object that can be added to a [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack). There are two types of [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) in VIQRC Mix & Match:

- Pin \- An orange, blue, or red roughly cylindrical object with a diameter of approximately 3.15” (80mm), height of 4.5” (116mm), and a weight of approximately 2.5 ounces (71g).
- Beam \- A gray, roughly rectangular object with a size of 9.88” (251mm) x 4.88” (124mm) x 1.97” (50mm) and a weight of approximately 6 ounces (170g).

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/Pins.png)

Figure SO-1: Red, blue, and orange [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin)

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/Beam.png)

Figure SO-2: A [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam)

Stack \- A set of two or more [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject).

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/GamePiece-Connected.png)

Figure S-1: A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) of two [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin).

Starting Pin \- A [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) that begins the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) on a [Starting Pin Support](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpinsupport).

Starting Pin Support \- One of four (4) red or blue structures, built out of VEX IQ parts, that is attached to the [Field Perimeter](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldperimeter). Each [Starting Pin Support](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpinsupport) holds a [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) of its color at the beginning of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), and until the [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) is removed by a Robot.

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/Starting_Peg_(Not_Cleared).png)

Figure SPS-1: A [Starting Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpin).

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/Starting_Peg_(Cleared).png)

Figure SPS-2: A [Starting Pin Support](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpinsupport).

* * *

**# Scoring**

|     |     |
| --- | --- |
| Each [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) | 1 Point |
| Each [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) | 10 Points |
| Each 2-color [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) | 5-Point Bonus |
| Each 3-color [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) | 15-Point Bonus |
| Each [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) bonus | 10-Point Bonus |
| Each [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) on the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal) | 10-Point Bonus |
| Each [Cleared](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#cleared) [Starting Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpin) | 2 Points |
| Each [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) in contact with [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). See [<SC8>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc8). | 2 Points |

<SC1> All scoring statuses are evaluated after the Match ends, once all [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject), Field Elements, and [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) on the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) come to rest. See rule [<GG12>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg12) for more information and [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) details.

1. Referees should avoid contacting or moving [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) as much as possible while evaluating Scoring statuses. If an object must be moved to evaluate the status of another object, its status must be agreed upon by all [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) and the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee), and noted or recorded, before it is moved.
2. Referees should record counts based on verified scoring statuses evaluated after the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), using final positions of [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject), Field Elements, and [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). Points scored during a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) should not be deducted from a score, other than scoring which takes place after the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) due to continued [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) movement (see clause b of [<GG12>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg12)).

<SC2> All scoring statuses are evaluated visually by a Head Referee, to the best of their ability within the context of a given [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match)/event.

1. Referees and other event staff are not allowed to review any videos or pictures from the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). See [<T3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t3).
2. If there is a concern regarding the score of a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), only the [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) from that [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), not an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult), may share their questions with the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee). See [<T3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t3).

<SC3>A Scoring Object can be Connected to another Scoring Object to form a [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack). To qualify as [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected), the resulting [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) must be roughly vertical (i.e., the [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) goes ‘up’ and not sideways) and cannot be in contact with a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).

1. [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) can be [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) in two ways: up from the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) or [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal), or up from a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam).
2. A [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) if it is fully nested (see Figure SC3-1) with another [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) and neither the [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) nor the resulting [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is touching a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).
3. A [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) if it is fully nested to one or more [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) and/or the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal) and is not touching a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).



2. A [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) cannot be [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to another [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam).
3. A [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) may be [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to up to three (3) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) simultaneously if all [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) are fully nested with the [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam).
4. Each [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) that is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) directly to a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) is considered to be part of a separate [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack), and a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) may count as a color in up to three (3) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) simultaneously.
4. A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) that meets the requirements of the other clauses in this rule and is resting on one of the following Field Elements in a way that is more "up and down" than sideways should generally be considered as roughly vertical:




   - [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor)
   - [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone)
   - Any part of the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal)
   - The VEX IQ pieces that are attached to the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) around a [Square Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#squaregoal)
5. A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) that is leaning on / supported by a [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) that is not part of the [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) or a [Field Element](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldelements) other than those listed above should not be considered roughly vertical and should not count as [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) or a [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).
6. [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) contact with a lower [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) in a multi- [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) structure has no impact on the higher [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) in that structure for the purposes of clauses D & E. See <SE9> for an example.

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/Nested-Anno.png)

Figure SC3-1: Examples of nested and non-nested [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin).

Note: [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) cannot count as [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) or [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) in [Goals](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal) if they are not vertical. [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) that end the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) ‘knocked down’ or ‘tipped’ within the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), or that are not [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to other [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject), can only count toward the 2 points earned for a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) that ends the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) in contact with 2 or more [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject).

Note 2: A pair of [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) is considered fully nested if there’s no perceptable gap between the two objects, and neither object is being pushed away from the other by an external force or surface.

Significant Q&As:

- [Q&A 2664](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2664) \- Multiple scoring scenarios; Beam on floor generally leads to non-nested Pins
- [Q&A 2669](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2669) \- Scoring example with a Beam supported by the perimeter
- [Q&A 2679](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2679) \- A Beam can earn points if it’s Connected to the Standoff Goal with no Pins
- [Q&A 2716](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2716) \- Examples to clarify “fully nested” and “roughly vertical”
- [Q&A 2878](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2878) \- A “U-Beam” structure that’s sitting on the floor is usually not nested and worth 0 points
- [Q&A 2881](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2881) \- A “U-Beam” structure that’s sitting on a Load Zone (or the bottom of the Standoff Goal, or the IQ pieces around a Square Goal) can potentially be fully nested and count as Connected Scoring Objects and Stacks
- [Q&A 2917](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2917) \- If multiple objects in a single Stack are contacting the Floor, it can’t be considered ‘roughly vertical’ and is worth 0 points
- [Q&A 2986](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2986) \- An unscored object on top of a Stack doesn’t affect the Stack; A Stack leaning on an unconnected Pin or a Starting Pin Support isn’t Connected or Stacked
- [Q&A 3009](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/3009) \- If a complex multi-Stack structure isn’t nested to the Standoff Goal, the objects in those Stacks may still count as Connected or Stacked, but they count count as Placed on the Standoff Goal


<SC4> A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) that includes more than one color (blue, red, orange, or gray) of [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) receives additional points based on the number of colors in that [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack), up to three colors.

<SC5> A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is considered Placed in a Goal at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) if it meets all of the following criteria.

1. There are at least two (2) [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) in the [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).
2. No part of the [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is contacting a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).
3. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) meets one of the following criteria:




1. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is contacting the PET sheet and entirely within the center outline that defines the [Floor Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floorgoal) (maximum of four (4) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack)).
2. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is entirely within a [Square Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#squaregoal) (maximum of one (1) [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) per [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal)).
3. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is entirely within a < [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal) (maximum of three (3) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) per [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal)).
4. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is above the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal) in one of the following configurations:




      - The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal)
      - The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) up from a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) that is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal)
      - The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) up from a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) that is part of another [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) that is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal)

Significant Q&As:

- [Q&A 2714](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2714) \- Example scoring for a stack on the Standoff Goal and in contact with a Robot
- [Q&A 2717](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2717) \- Example scoring for a Stack that is Placed in the Floor Goal and connected down from a Beam that is Connected to the Standoff Goal
- [Q&A 2755](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2755) \- Clarification of “entirely within” a Goal

<SC6> A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) earns a Matching Goal bonus when one or more of the following criteria is met:

1. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) in a [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal) with a color that matches the bottom [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) in that [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).
2. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam).

Each [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) can earn a maximum of one (1) [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) bonus.

Significant Q&As:

- [Q&A 2665](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2665) \- One Pin connected to a Beam counts as a Stack
- [Q&A 2873](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2873) \- Only a Stack can earn a Matching Goal bonus, and a Stack consists of 2 or more Connected Scoring Objects
- [Q&A 2887](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2887) \- One Pin placed on the Standoff Goal doesn’t count as Connected or a Stack, and is worth 0 points
- [Q&A 2894](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2894) \- Scoring example for a “U-Beam” on the Standoff Goal

<SC7>A Starting Pin is Cleared if no part of its Starting Pin Support is within the volume of a [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

<SC8> A [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) will receive 2 points for ending the Match in contact with Scoring Objects in the following scenarios:

1. The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is directly contacting two or more [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject).
2. The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is directly contacting a [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) that is fully nested with one or more additional [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject).

Significant Q&As:

- [Q&A 2758](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2758) -Multiple Robots can contact the same Scoring Object or Stack
- [Q&A 2759](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2759) \- Pins on Starting Pin Supports count toward this rule

* * *

**# Scoring Examples**

<SE1> All [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) in this example are [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected), and none are [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) in a [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal). This example is scored as 6 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin), 1 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam), and three 3-color [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) with a [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus.

|     |     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/SC8-1.png) | Scoring Category | Points | Quantity | Subtotal |
| [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) | 1 point | 6 | 6 |
| [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) | 10 points | 1 | 10 |
| 3-color [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) | 15 points | 3 | 45 |
| [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus | 10 points | 3 | 30 |
| Total Points for this example | **91** |

<SE2> All [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) in this example are [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected), and none are [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) in a [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal). This example is scored as 6 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin), 1 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam), and three 3-color [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) with a [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus.

| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

<SE3> The top [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) in this example is not [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to the [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam), and is supported by a [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) that is not part of that [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack). All other [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) are [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected), and none are [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) in a [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal). This example is scored as 4 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) Pins, 1 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam), and two 3-color [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) with a [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus.

| [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) | 1 point | 4 | 4 |
| [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) | 10 points | 1 | 10 |

| [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus | 10 points | 2 | 20 |
| Total Points for this example | **64** |

<SE4> The [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) in this example is not [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected), but all of the [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) are; no [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) are [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) in a [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal). This example is scored as 4 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) and two 2-color [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) not [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) in a [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal) and not [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam).

| 2 -color [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) | 5 points | 2 | 10 |
| Total Points for this example | **14** |

<SE5> Because none of these [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) are vertical, nothing in this example counts as [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) or as a [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack). No other points are scored. This example would not receive a score.

<SE6> The [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) in this example are [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected), [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) in a [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal), and [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) on the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal). This example is scored as 3 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin), one 3-color [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) with a [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus, and [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) on the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal).

| Total Points for this example | **38** |

<SE7> All [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) in this example are [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected), and all three [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) are [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) on the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal) via the [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam). This example is scored as 6 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin), 1 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam), three 3-color [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) with a [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus and three [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) on the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal).

<SE8> The [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) in this example are nested together, but part of the [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is in contact with a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). None of the [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) qualify as [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected). This example is scored as a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) in contact with [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

|     |     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/SE8.png) | Scoring Category | Points | Quantity | Subtotal |
| [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) | 1 point | 0 | 0 |
| 3-color [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) | 15 points | 0 | 0 |
| [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) in contact with [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) | 2 points | 1 | 2 |
| Total Points for this example | **2** |

<SE9> All of the [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) in this example are nested together, but a [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) in one of the [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is in contact with a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). The [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) in the one [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) that is in contact with the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) do not qualify as [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to each other or to the [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam); however, as described in clause F of [<SC3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc3) the other [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) still qualify as roughly vertical. This example is scored as 4 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin), 1 [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam), two 3-color [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) with a [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus, and a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) in contact with [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

|     |     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/SE9.png) | Scoring Category | Points | Quantity | Subtotal |
| [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) | 1 point | 4 | 4 |
| [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) | 10 points | 1 | 10 |
| 3-color [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) | 15 points | 2 | 30 |
| [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus | 10 points | 2 | 20 |
| [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) in contact with [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) | 2 points | 1 | 2 |
| Total Points for this example | **66** |

<SE10> All of the [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) in this example are nested together, but the [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) is in contact with a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). Because the [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) is part of all three [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack), none of the [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) qualify as [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected). This example is scored as a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) in contact with [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

|     |     |     |     |     |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| ![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/SE10.png) | Scoring Category | Points | Quantity | Subtotal |
| [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) | 1 point | 0 | 0 |
| [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) | 10 points | 0 | 0 |
| 3-color [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) | 15 points | 0 | 0 |
| [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus | 10 points | 0 | 0 |
| [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) in contact with [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) | 2 points | 1 | 2 |
| Total Points for this example | **2** |

* * *

**# Safety Rules**

<S1>Stay safe, don’t damage the Field. If, at any time, the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) operation or [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) actions are deemed unsafe or have damaged any Field Elements or [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject), the offending [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may be [Disabled](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disablement) and/or [Disqualified](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) at the [Head Referee’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) discretion. The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) will require re-inspection before it may again take the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field).

Note: [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may not step onto the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) at any time. If a [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) requires stepping onto the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) during pre- [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) setup, this will be considered a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [<S1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#s1), [<GG3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg3), and/or [<SG1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sg1). The [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) may be removed from the current [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) at the [Head Referee’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) discretion.

Violation Notes: [Major Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation) should be reported to and/or discussed with the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) during the event, and should be reported to the REC Foundation Rules and Conduct Committee following the event.

<S2>Students must be accompanied by an Adult. No [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) may attend a VEX IQ Robotics Competition event without a responsible [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) supervising them. The [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) must obey all rules and be careful to not violate [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student)-centered policies, but must be present for the full duration of the event in the case of an emergency. [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule may result in removal from the event.

Violation Notes: [<S2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#s2) [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) should be reported to the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) during the event, and should be reported to the REC Foundation Rules and Conduct Committee following the event.

<S3>Each Student Team member must have a completed participant release form on file for the event and season. A [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) member cannot participate in an event without a completed release form on file.

* * *

**# General Rules**

<G1>Treat everyone with respect. All [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are expected to conduct themselves in a respectful and professional manner while competing in VEX IQ Robotics Competition events. If a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) or any of its members ( [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) or any [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) associated with the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team)) are disrespectful or uncivil to event staff, volunteers, or fellow competitors, they may be [Disqualified](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) from a current or upcoming [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) conduct pertaining to [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) may also impact a [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) eligibility for judged awards. Repeated or extreme [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) could result in a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) being [Disqualified](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) from an entire event, depending on the severity of the situation.

This rule exists alongside the REC Foundation Code of Conduct. [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of the Code of Conduct can be considered a [Major Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation) of [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) and can result in [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) from a current [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), an upcoming [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), an entire event, or (in extreme cases) an entire competition season. The Code of Conduct can be found [here](https://viqrc-kb.recf.org/hc/en-us/articles/9778593540247-Code-of-Conduct).

- Event attendees are not allowed to record audio or video of [Teams’](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) discussions with [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) or other event staff/volunteers.

More information regarding the event Code of Conduct process can be found at the [RECF Library](https://viqrc-kb.recf.org/hc/en-us/articles/16943810308503-Event-Code-of-Conduct-Process).

We all can contribute to creating a fun and inclusive event experience for all event attendees. Some examples include:

When dealing with difficult and stressful situations, it is…

- Okay for [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to be gracious and supportive when your [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) partner makes a mistake.
- Not okay for [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to harass, tease, or be disrespectful to your [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) partner when a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) does not go your way.

When a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) does not understand a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) ruling or score, it is…

- Okay for [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) to consult with a [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) to discuss a ruling per the process outlined in [<T3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t3) in a calm and respectful manner.
- Not okay for [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) to continue arguing with the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) after a decision has been finalized, or for [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to approach a [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) with ruling/scoring concerns.

When [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are getting ready for an upcoming [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), it is…

- Okay for [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) in an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) to develop a game strategy that utilizes the strengths of both [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) to cooperatively solve the game.
- Not okay for one [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) in an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) to ask another [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to sit in a corner during the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) or to intentionally play beneath their abilities.

Violation Notes: Any [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) may be considered a [Major Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation) and should be addressed on a case-by-case basis. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) at risk of a [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) [Major Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation) due to multiple disrespectful or uncivil behaviors will usually receive a “final warning”, although the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) is not required to provide one. All [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) [Major Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation)/ [Disqualifications](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) should be reported to and/or discussed with the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) during the event, and should be reported to the REC Foundation Rules and Conduct Committee following the event.

<G2>VIQRC is a student-centered program. [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) should not make decisions about the [Robot’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) build, design, or gameplay, and should not provide an unfair advantage by providing ‘help’ that is beyond the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student)’ independent abilities. [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) must be prepared to demonstrate an active understanding of their [Robot’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) design, construction, and programming to judges or event staff. [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) should build, design, and code the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) with minimal [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) involvement.

Some amount of [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) mentorship, teaching, and/or guidance is an expected and encouraged facet of VEX competitions. No one is born an expert in robotics! However, obstacles should always be viewed as teaching opportunities, not problems for an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to solve for the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team).

When building or designing the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), it is…

- Okay for an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to help a [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) consider why something failed, so it can be improved.
- Not okay for an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to provide step by step instructions or photos for the [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) to copy.

When a mechanism falls off, it is…

- Okay for an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to help a [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) consider why it failed, so it can be improved.
- Not okay for an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to investigate or put the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) back together.

When a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) encounters a complex programming concept, it is…

- Okay for an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to guide a [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) through a flowchart to understand its logic.
- Not okay for an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to write a premade command for that [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) to copy / paste.

During [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) play, it is…

- Okay for an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to provide cheerful, positive encouragement as a spectator.
- Not okay for an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to explicitly shout step-by-step commands from the audience.

This rule operates in tandem with the [REC Foundation Student Centered Policy](https://viqrc-kb.recf.org/hc/en-us/articles/9778591033879-Student-Centered-Policy), which is available in the REC Library for [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to reference throughout the season.

Violation Notes: Potential [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule will be reviewed on a case-by-case basis. By definition, all [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule become [Score Affecting](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoreaffecting) as soon as a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) which was built or programmed by an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) scores points in a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). All reported and/or suspected [<G2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g2) [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) should be reported to the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) during the event, and should be reported to the REC Foundation Rules and Conduct Committee following the event.

Significant Q&As:

- [Q&A 2819](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2819) \- Adults cannot transcribe or type notebook entries for Students

<G3>Use common sense. When reading and applying the various rules in this document, please remember that common sense always applies in the VEX IQ Robotics Competition.

Some examples may include:

- If there is an obvious typographical error (such as “per [<T5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t5)” instead of “per [<GG5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg5)”), this does not mean that the error should be taken literally until corrected in a future update.
- Understand the realities of the VEX IQ [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) construction system. For example, if a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) could hover above the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) for a whole [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), that would create loopholes in many of the rules. But… they can’t. So… don’t worry about it.
- When in doubt, if there is no rule prohibiting an action, it is generally legal. However, if you have to ask whether a given action would violate [<S1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#s1), [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1), or [<T1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t1) then that’s probably a good indication that it is outside the spirit of the competition. On the other hand, if there’s not a rule that makes a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) part legal, it’s not allowed.
- In general, [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) will be given the “benefit of the doubt” in the case of accidental or edge-case rules infractions. However, there is a limit to this allowance, and repeated or strategic infractions will still be penalized.

<G4>All work must represent the skill level of the Students on the Team. The [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) design, [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), coding, strategy, and ongoing work must represent the skill level of the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) currently on the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team).

- [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) must avoid academic dishonesty and should not copy a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) or mechanism that has been provided for them. This includes, but is not limited to, the use of instructions, pictures & videos, notebooks, CAD designs, and/or any other documentation useful to the design process provided by anyone that is not a [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) on the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) (including [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) on another [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team)).
- [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may be inspired by designs by other [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), and use an idea from someone else to spark innovation, but are expected to document and demonstrate this in their engineering notebook alongside evidence of iteration. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are required to present this evidence if asked to do so by a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) inspector, [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee), [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner), or Judge.

  - Using elements of another design as a starting point is acceptable if the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is capable of demonstrating evidence of iteration, innovation, and/or modification that makes the design uniquely their own. Documentation should clearly demonstrate the idea that was used for inspiration, and how it was changed for the final implementation on the [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). It should be clear that this final implementation is not an exact copy of ANY other original design.
  - Failure to demonstrate evidence of iteration, innovation, and/or modification will result in a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation).

- [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may use [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) plans and code (e.g., the annual Hero Bot, VEXcode configurations, etc.) provided by VEX Robotics or the RECF, but are encouraged to use these [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), mechanisms, and code only as a starting point that [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) modify, improve, or replace as their skills increase. Plans provided by VEX Robotics or the RECF are the only legal plans available for use in competition.
- This rule still applies to [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) within the same school, organization, or club. [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) and/or code sets that are identical or substantially similar to one another across [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) within the same school/organization/club will be considered in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule, regardless of whether they compete in the same or different events. Clause D does not apply in situations where both/all [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are using the unmodified Hero Bot design, as allowed by clause C of this rule.

For more information, including acceptable and unacceptable examples of mechanical design, construction, coding, and strategy solutions, please refer to the [Student Centered Policy](https://kb.roboticseducation.org/hc/en-us/articles/5449868745367-Student-Centered-Policy) in the RECF Library.

The VEX Robotics Competition and the Robotics Education & Competition Foundation (RECF) recognize that many third-party individuals and organizations produce and distribute [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) designs, instructions, and/or other materials that are not under our direct control. We cannot legally regulate or restrict the activities of these external entities. However, when [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) use these resources in ways that violate the spirit and letter of the VEX Robotics Game Manual—particularly Rules [<G2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g2) and [<G4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g4)—they undermine the core mission of the program: to provide [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) with hands-on opportunities to learn, design, and innovate.

While it is never our intent to punish [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student), we can legally regulate and restrict the activities of the [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) in our competitions, and we must preserve the fairness, educational value, and integrity of the competition. Therefore, [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) found to be in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of these rules will be held accountable to the strictest interpretations of [<G2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g2) and [<G4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g4).

It is the responsibility of each [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to be able to explain and defend the design, construction, and programming of their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) if questioned by referees, inspectors, [Event Partners](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner), or judges. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) should be prepared to describe their design process, justify design decisions, and demonstrate a full understanding of how their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) and code function.

**If a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is unable, for any reason, to provide reasonable evidence (when requested by event staff) that their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) and code are the result of their own work, it is appropriate to assume that the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [<G2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g2) and/or [<G4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g4).**

Event organizers cannot reasonably know the origins of every design or independently verify whether a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) was created from scratch, purchased online, or copied from pictures of another [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) design. When questions of authenticity arise, the only direct and fair approach is to require [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) to explain and defend their work. This is not unlike academic honesty concerns in schools, and intellectual property concerns in business. By requiring [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) to defend their designs, we ensure that they are developing not only technical skills, but effective communication skills and accountability, as well.

Consequences may include disqualification from matches, removal from events, and/or escalation of the investigation to VEX Robotics and the RECF for further disciplinary action, which may include sanctions up to and including removal from the program.

Event staff should bear in mind [<G3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g3), and use common sense when enforcing this rule. It is not the intent to actively hunt for [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule, compare every [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) at an event to all other known [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) designs, or closely question every team at an event about their [Robot's](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) code. This rule is a set of tools for use if potential [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) are noted by or reported to event staff, and it is expected that most [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) will never be required to defend their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) design or code.

[Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) or individuals who deliberately weaponize, manipulate, or falsely report [<G4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g4) [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) for competitive gain or to harass another Team may be subject to a separate RECF Code of Conduct investigation. Misuse of this rule is considered a serious [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation).

Significant Q&As:

  - [Q&A 2930](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2930) \- Additional info on how much change to a mechanism is “enough”

Violation Notes:

  - [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) believed to be in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule should be reported to the Judge Advisor, [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee), or [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) for further investigation in coordination with the RSM. Based on the investigation the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may be removed from further [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), have their Robot Skills Challenge scores removed, and/or be removed from consideration from judged awards.
  - [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule will be evaluated on a case-by-case basis, in tandem with the RECF Student Centered Policy as noted in [<G2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g2), and the REC Foundation Code of Conduct as noted in [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#winpoints). All reported and/or suspected [<G4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g4) [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) should be reported to the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) during the event, and should be reported to the RECF Rules and Conduct Committee following the event.

<G5>Each Student can only belong to one Team. Each Team must include [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers), [Coder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team)(s), [Designer](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team)(s), and [Builder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team)(s). Many also include notebooker(s). No [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) may fulfill any of these roles for more than one VEX IQ Robotics Competition [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) in a given competition season. [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) may have more than one role on the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), e.g., the [Designer](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may also be the [Builder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), the [Coder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), and a [Drive Team Member](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammember).

  - [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) members may only move from one [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to another for non-strategic reasons outside of the [Team's](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) control.

    - Examples of permissible moves may include, but are not limited to, changing schools, conflicts within a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), or combining/splitting [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team).
    - Examples of strategic moves in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule may include, but are not limited to, one [Coder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) “switching” [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) in order to program multiple [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), one [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) designing multiple teams’ [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), or one [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) writing the Engineering Notebook for multiple [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team).
    - If a [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) leaves a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to join another [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), [<G4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g4) still applies to the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) remaining on the previous [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team). For example, if a [Coder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) leaves a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), then that [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) must still represent the skill level of the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) without that [Coder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team). One way to accomplish this would be to ensure that the [Coder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) teaches or trains a “replacement” [Coder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) in their absence.
    - Points ii and iii are intended to represent real-world situations that are found in industry engineering. If a vital member of a professional engineering team were to suddenly leave, the remaining members of the team should still be capable of working on / maintaining their project.

  - When a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) qualifies for a Championship event (e.g., States, Nationals, Worlds, etc.) the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) on the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) attending the Championship event are expected to be the same [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) on the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) that was awarded the spot. [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) can be added as support to the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), but may not be added as [Drivers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) or [Coders](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) for the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team).
    - An exception is allowed if only one (1) member of the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is able to attend the event. The [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) can make a single substitution of a [Drive Team Member](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammember) or [Coder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) for the Championship event with another [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student), even if that [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) has competed on a different [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team). This [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) will now be a member of this new [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) and may not substitute back to the original [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) during the season.

Note: [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) cannot “borrow” [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) from other [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to serve as [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers), [Coders](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), [Designers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) and [Builders](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) or notebookers. However, [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) can add permanent members throughout the season under the guidelines of this rule.

Violation Notes: [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) believed to be in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule should be reported to the Judge Advisor, [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee), or [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) for further investigation in coordination with the RSM.

[Event Partners](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) should bear in mind [<G3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g3), and use common sense when enforcing this rule. It is not the intent to punish a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) who may change [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) members over the course of a season due to illness, changing schools, conflicts within a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), etc.

[Event Partners](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) and referees are not expected to keep a roster of any [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) who has ever been a [Drive Team Member](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammember) for one day. This rule is intended to block any instance of loaning or sharing [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) members for the sole purpose of gaining a competitive advantage.

* * *

**# General Game Rules**

<GG1>Drivers drive your Robot, and stay in the Driver Station. During a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) may only be operated by that [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Drivers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) and/or software running on the [Robot’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) control system. Each [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may send up to three (3) [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) to their [Driver Station](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driverstation) for a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match): two (2) [Drivers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) and one (1) Loader. Those [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) must remain in their [Driver Station](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driverstation), except when legally interacting with their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) per [<GG10>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg10).

1. [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) are prohibited from any of the following actions during a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match):




1. Using any sort of communication device in the [Driver Station](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driverstation). Non-headphone devices with communication features turned off (e.g. a phone in airplane mode or a walkie talkie turned off) are allowed. If communication features are needed for translation apps during post- [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) discussions, it should not be considered a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation).
2. Standing or sitting on any sort of object during a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), regardless of whether the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) is on the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) or elevated, except as required by an official [accommodation request](https://kb.roboticseducation.org/hc/en-us/articles/22353712963095-Needs-based-Special-Accommodations) that has been approved by the REC Foundation.
3. Using additional materials to simplify the game challenge during a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).
4. To ensure that [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) are aware of verbal calls during a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) (as an application of rules [<T1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t1), [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1), [<S1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#s1), and [<G3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g3)), powered headphones, earbuds, and/or passive earpieces connected to electronic devices cannot be worn/used in the [Driver Station](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driverstation) except as required by an official [accommodation request](https://kb.roboticseducation.org/hc/en-us/articles/22353712963095-Needs-based-Special-Accommodations) that has been approved by the REC Foundation.

Point iii is intended to refer to non- [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot)-related items that directly influence gameplay, such as using a ramp to assist with the [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone). Provided no other rules are violated, and the items do not pose any safety or [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) damage risks, the following examples are not considered [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [<GG1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg1):

   - Materials used before or after a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), such as a pre- [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) alignment aid
   - Strategic aids, such as a whiteboard or clipboard
   - Earplugs, gloves, or other personal accessories

4.
