At league events in which Teams may submit [Robot Skills Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillschallenge) scores across multiple sessions, the Robot Skills scores (combined highest [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) and [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) scores) used for rankings will be calculated from [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) within the same session.

For example, consider the following scores for a hypothetical [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) across two league event sessions:

This [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) would have a Robot Skills score of 72 for this event’s rankings, and their scores from Session 2 would be used for the event and global tiebreakers listed in [<T17>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t17) and [<T18>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t18).

|  | [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) | [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) | Robot Skills Score |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| Session 1 | 25 | 45 | 70 |
| Session 2 | 30 | 42 | 72 |

**# Appendix B - Student-Friendly Appendix**

## Using this Appendix

Hey [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student)!

Welcome to the VEX IQ Robotics Competition. We’re excited to see you play Mix & Match! We know that learning new things can be hard, and that the “big game manual” can be kind of a lot. So, we’re here to help!

You and your teammates can start here and work together to learn about the important parts of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), how to earn points, study basic rules, and see different ways to play the game. But these are only some of the rules of this year’s game, and you will need to know them all! So after you understand everything here, and before you go to your first event, head over to the official game manual to make sure you understand all of the rules.

We hope that you have fun, make lots of friends, and work together to build your best [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) ever! Have an awesome season!

* * *

Hi [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult)!

This unofficial version of the VEX IQ Robotics Competition manual is a print-friendly resource for you and your [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to help introduce [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) to this season’s game, Mix & Match.

It’s very important to note that this is NOT a replacement for reading the official manual in its entirety. We encourage you to use this Appendix to support [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) members who may be overwhelmed by the full game manual, and use it to aid in building a basic understanding of the game. Once [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) are comfortable with this appendix and the rules outlined here, you should transition them to reading and using the full game manual, where they will gain a full-depth comprehension of the VEX IQ Robotics Competition.

We hope that you’ll find this guide helpful and that more [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) feel welcomed, supported, and empowered to join your [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team).

Your Robotics friends,

The VEX Robotics Competition Game Design Committee

## Important Rules

It’s very important to understand that all of the rules of Mix and Match must be followed, not just by [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student), but by [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult), too. The choices that [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) and [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) make go hand-in-hand, so be sure to follow the rules together.

Treat everyone with respect. [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1)

- Be kind and do your best. This is one of the most important parts of VEX IQ.
- Be respectful. It’s okay for [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) and [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to disagree, but it’s never okay to be disrespectful.
- Be a good sport. Think about how you make other people feel.
- Include everyone. [Alliances](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) should always work together to come up with a plan, and telling another person how they have to play the game is not allowed.

VIQRC is a student-centered program. [<G2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g2)

- The [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student)-Centered Policy is very important because VEX IQ is a competition for [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student).
- This means that the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) come up with the ideas, build the [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), write the code, troubleshoot, and compete.
- [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) can teach, but can’t do the work. [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) should give [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) tips, not answers, and cannot directly work on [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), code, engineering notebooks, or in- [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) strategy.
- [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) should respectfully speak up when an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) is doing too much, and give a reminder that when it comes to VEX IQ, [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student)-Centered is a rule all the time and everywhere.

## How do you play Mix & Match?

Mix & Match is a game where two [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) work together to make [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) of [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) and [Beams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) to score points. During each Match, all of the points that both [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) earn are added together to come up with a [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) score. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are ranked based on their scores in [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), and the top [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) will compete in the [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) to determine a Teamwork Champion.

[Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) can also play in [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) to see how well their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) does in a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) by itself. There are two kinds of [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch), one for driving the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) (called a [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch)) and another (called an [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch)) where the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) can only run using pre-written programs created by the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) on the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team).

### Game Pieces and Goals

**Pins and Beams**

- There are 36 [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) in each [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) can be orange, blue, or red.
- Some [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) begin on the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), some are put into the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) by Loaders, and each [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) can start with a [Preload](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#preload) [<SG5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sg5).
- There are two gray [Beams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) that start the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) on the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field).

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/Pins.png)

Red, blue, and orange [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin)

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/Beam.png)

A [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam)

**Goals**

- There are four (4) types of [Goals](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal): Square, Triangle, Floor, and Standoff.

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/RampGoal.png)

Figure G-1: A [Square Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#squaregoal).

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/FenceGoal.png)

Figure G-2: A < [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal).

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/FloorGoal.png)

Figure G-3: A [Floor Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floorgoal) and [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal).

**Starting Pins**

- 4 [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) start the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) on [Starting Pin Supports](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpinsupport).

![](https://content.vexrobotics.com/docs/25-26/viqrc-mix-and-match/online-manual/images/Starting_Peg_(Cleared)1.png)

A [Starting Pin Support](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpinsupport).

## How to Earn Points

Robots build Stacks [<SC3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc3)

- Make [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) of two or more [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) anywhere on the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) to earn points
- Make [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) with more colors to earn more points [<SC4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc4)
- Include [Beams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) in [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) to earn even more points [<SC3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc3)

Robots put Stacks into or onto Goals [<SC5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc5)

- [Place](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) into or on [Matching Goals](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) to earn more points [<SC6>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc6)

[Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) can touch two or more [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) ( [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) or [Beams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam)) at the end of the Match to score two points.

[Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) can [Clear](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#cleared) [Starting Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpin) to earn points [<SC7>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc7)

## Robot Rules

Robots can’t get bigger than 11 inches by 20 inches during a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), but can follow rule [<SG3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sg3) to get taller than 15 inches after the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) starts.

Your [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) has to be designed, built, and programmed by the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) on your [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), not by [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) [<R2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#r2), using only VEX IQ parts [<R14>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#r14).

Drive Team

Three [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) make up the Drive Team for each [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match):

- [Driver](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) 1 - Drives the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) for the first 30 seconds [<GG11>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg11)
- [Driver](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) 2 - Drives the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) for the last 30 seconds
- Loader - [Places](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) into the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) for the whole [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) [<SG6>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sg6)

Your [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Driver](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) 1, [Driver](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) 2, and Loader can be different for each [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), but all of them have to be members of your [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team). [<G5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g5) and <GG11f>

Referees and Scoring

- [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) should know who the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) is each [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) [<T1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t1).
- Robots must stop moving at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) [<GG12>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg12) and can end the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) early [<GG13>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg13).
- Scores are added up at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) and are shown to the [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) by a Scorekeeper or [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) [<SC1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc1).
- Only [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) can talk to the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) about any questions they have from the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), and have to do it right after the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) are not allowed to be a part of this conversation. [<SC2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc2)
- What the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) says goes. [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) are encouraged to respectfully ask questions after a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), but it’s not okay to argue after the Referee makes their final decision [<T3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t3).

##### Adult

Adult \- Anyone who is not a [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) or another defined term (e.g., [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee)).

##### Alliance

Alliance \- A pre-assigned grouping of two (2) [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) that are paired together during a given [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

##### Alliance Score

Alliance Score \- Points scored in a [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) that are awarded to both [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team).

##### Disablement

Disablement \- A penalty applied to a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) for a safety [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation). During [Disablement](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disablement), a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is no longer allowed to operate their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), and the [Drivers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) will be asked to place their Controller down. A [Disablement](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disablement) is not the same as a [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification).

##### Disqualification

Disqualification \- A penalty applied to a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) for a rule [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) (see [<GG6>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg6) for more details). If a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) receives a [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) in a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) will notify the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) of their [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). At the [Head Referee’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) discretion, repeated [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) and/or [Disqualifications](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) for a single [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may lead to its [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) for the entire event.

##### Driver

Driver \- A [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) member who stands in the [Driver Station](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driverstation) and is responsible for operating and controlling that [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). Up to two [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) members may fulfill this role in a given [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) (see [<GG1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg1)), and there is no requirement that the same [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) serve as [Drivers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) in multiple [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

##### Driver Station

Driver Station \- A region beside the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) where the [Drivers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) must remain during their [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) unless legally interacting with their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). The [Driver Stations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driverstation) are represented by the red and blue lines in Figure FO-3.

##### Drive Team Members

Drive Team Members \- The two [Drivers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) and one Loader who participate in a given [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) as representatives of their [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team). No [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) may fill more than one role on a Drive Team in the same [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

- [Driver](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) 1 - Drives the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) until the mid- [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) Driver switch (see [<GG11>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg11))
- Driver 2 - Drives the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) after the mid- [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) Driver switch (see [<GG11>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg11))
- Loader - Introduces [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) into the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) for the whole [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match)

##### Field

Field \- The entire playing [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), being six (6) [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) tiles wide by eight (8) [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) tiles long (totaling forty-eight (48) [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) tiles), including the [Field Perimeter](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldperimeter).

##### Field Element

Field Element \- The [Field Perimeter](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldperimeter), [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor), PVC pipes, and VEX IQ pieces which comprise and/or are attached to the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field).

##### Field Perimeter

Field Perimeter \- The outer part of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), made up of four (4) outside corners and twenty-four (24) straight sections.

##### Floor

Floor \- The interior flat part of the playing [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), made up of the forty-eight (48) [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) tiles that are within the [Field Perimeter](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldperimeter).

##### Game Design Committee (GDC)

Game Design Committee (GDC) \- The creators of VIQRC Mix & Match, and authors of this Game Manual. The GDC is the only official source for rules clarifications and Q&A responses; see Section 1.

##### License Plate

License Plate \- A physical component on the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) that displays the [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) VEX IQ Robotics Competition number. Each [License Plate](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#licenseplate) must have a length and height of 3.5” x 1.5” (88.9mm x 38.1mm) and must not exceed a width of 0.25” (6.35mm) per [<R6>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#r6).

##### Match

Match \- A set time period, consisting of [Autonomous Periods](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomousperiod) and/or [Driver Controlled Periods](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivercontrolledperiod), during which [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) play a defined version of Mix & Match to earn points. See Sections 3 & 4.

##### Autonomous Period

Autonomous Period \- A time period during which [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) operate and react only to sensor inputs and/or commands pre-programmed by the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) into the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) control system.

##### Driver Controlled Period

Driver Controlled Period \- A time period during which [Drivers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) operate their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).

##### Robot

Robot \- A machine that has passed inspection, designed by [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) members to execute one or more tasks autonomously and/or by remote control from [Drivers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver).

##### Student

Student \- Anyone born after May 1, 2010 (i.e., who will be 15 or younger at VEX Worlds 2026). Eligibility may also be granted based on a disability that has delayed education by at least one year. [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) are the individuals who design, build, repair, and program the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) with minimal [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) assistance.

##### Elementary School Student

Elementary School Student – Any [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) born after May 1, 2013 (i.e., who will be 12 or younger at VEX Worlds 2026). [Elementary School Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#elementaryschoolstudent) may “play up” and compete as [Middle School Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#middleschoolstudent).

##### Middle School Student

Middle School Student \- Any eligible [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) that is not an [Elementary School Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#elementaryschoolstudent).

##### Team

Team \- Three or more [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) make up a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team). To participate in an official VEX IQ Robotics Competition event, a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) must first register on RobotEvents.com and receive a VEX IQ Robotics Competition [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) number. A [Team's](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) unique number identifies their organization and their [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) within that organization. Each [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) must build their own [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), create their own code, and maintain their own Engineering Notebook if they choose to use one.

- A [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is classified as an Elementary School [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) if all members are [Elementary School Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#elementaryschoolstudent).
- A [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is classified as a Middle School [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) if any member is a [Middle School Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#middleschoolstudent), or if the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is made up of [Elementary School Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#elementaryschoolstudent) who declare themselves as “playing up” as [Middle School Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#middleschoolstudent) by registering their [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) as a Middle School [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team).
- Once a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) has competed in an event as a Middle School [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), that [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may not change to an Elementary School [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) for the remainder of the season. If a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) mistakenly registers as an Elementary School [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) but is ineligible for that age group, their registration may be revised mid-season with RSM assistance; all prior qualifications for the season will be lost.
- [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may be associated with schools, community/youth organizations, or a group of neighborhood [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student).

In the context of this Game Manual, [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) contain three types of [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) roles related to [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) build, design, and coding. See [<G2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g2) and [<G4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g4) for more information. [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) may not fulfill any of these roles.

##### Builder

Builder \- The [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student)(s) on the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) who assemble(s) the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) are permitted to teach the [Builder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#builder)(s) associated concepts, but should never work on the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).

##### Coder

Coder \- The [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student)(s) on the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) who write(s) the computer code that is downloaded onto the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) are permitted to teach the [Coder](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#coder)(s) associated concepts, but should never work on the code that goes on the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).

##### Designer

Designer \- The [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student)(s) on the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) who design(s) the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) to be built for competition. [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) are permitted to teach the [Designer](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#designer)(s) associated concepts, but should never work on the design of the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).

##### Violation

Violation \- The act of breaking a rule in the Game Manual.

Some rules include [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) Notes in red italicized text to denote special circumstances or provide additional clarifications. If no [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) Notes are found in a given rule, then it should be assumed that the default definitions above apply.

To determine whether a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) may have been [Score Affecting](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoreaffecting), check whether the [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) directly contributed to increasing the score of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). If it did not increase the [Alliance’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) score, then the [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) was not [Score Affecting](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoreaffecting), and it was very likely a [Minor Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#minorviolation).

##### Minor Violation

Minor Violation \- A [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) which does not result in a [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification).

- Accidental, momentary, or otherwise non- [Score Affecting](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoreaffecting) [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) are usually [Minor Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#minorviolation).
- [Minor Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#minorviolation) usually result in a verbal notification from the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) during the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), which should serve to inform the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) that a rule is being Violated before it escalates to a [Major Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation).

##### Major Violation

Major Violation \- A [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) which results in a [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification).

- Unless otherwise noted in a rule, all [Score Affecting](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoreaffecting) [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) are [Major Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation).
- If noted in the rule, egregious or strategic [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) or intentional actions that result in [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) may also be [Major Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation).
- Multiple [Minor Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#minorviolation) within a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) or tournament may escalate to a [Major Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation) at the [Head Referee’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) discretion or as specified in a rule.

##### Score Affecting

Score Affecting \- A [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) which improves an [Alliance’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) score at the end of a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

- Multiple [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) within a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) can cumulatively become [Score Affecting](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoreaffecting).
- When evaluating whether a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) was [Score Affecting](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoreaffecting), [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) will focus primarily on any [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) actions that were directly related to the [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation).
- Determining whether a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) was [Score Affecting](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoreaffecting) can only be done once the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) is complete and the scores have been calculated. [Minor Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#minorviolation) carry over into [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) unless otherwise specified within a rule.
- CoC-related Violation \- A [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of a rule that relates to the RECF Code of Conduct and related processes. For VIQRC, the included rules are: [<S2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#s2), [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1), [<G2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g2), [<G4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g4), [<G5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g5), [<R1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#r1) through [<R4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#r4), and [Major Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation) of [<S1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#s1).




  - Potential [CoC-related Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) should be brought to the attention of the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner), and resolved through the Code of Conduct Reporting Process in coordination with the [Score Affecting](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoreaffecting), [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee), Judge Advisor, and RECF Regional Support Manager. Follow-up investigations are conducted by the RECF Rules & Conduct Committee (RCC). Penalties for confirmed [CoC-related Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) can range from single- [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) [Disqualifications](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) to removal from the program.

##### Connected

Connected \- A [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) status. See [<SC3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc3).

##### Cleared

Cleared \- A [Starting Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpin) status. See [<SC7>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc7).

##### Goal

Goal \- A place where [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) can be [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed). There are four (4) varieties of [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal) in VIQRC Mix & Match:

##### Square Goal

Square Goal \- A segment of the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) in a corner of the long side of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) opposite from the audience. Each [Square Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#squaregoal) is bordered by the inside of the [Field Perimeter](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldperimeter) and the inside edges of the VEX IQ pieces connected to the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor). Each [Square Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#squaregoal) has a color, red or blue, determined by its VEX IQ pieces and PET sheet. Each [Square Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#squaregoal) can hold a maximum of one (1) [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).

##### Floor Goal

Floor Goal \- A segment of the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) in the center of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) surrounding the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal). The [Floor Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floorgoal) is defined by the center, white-outlined portion of the PET sheet connected to the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) underneath the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal), and includes that white line. The [Floor Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floorgoal) can hold a maximum of four (4) [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).

##### Triangle Goal

Triangle Goal \- A segment of the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) in a corner of the long side of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) closest to the audience. Each < [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal) is bordered by the inside of the [Field Perimeter](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldperimeter) and the inside of the PVC pipe that spans the corner of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field). Each < [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal) has a color, red or blue, determined by its VEX IQ pieces, PVC pipe, and PET sheet. Each < [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal) can hold a maximum of three (3) [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).

##### Standoff Goal

Standoff Goal \- The orange plastic structure mounted to the center of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) with IQ pins or screws.

##### Load

Load \- The act of legally introducing a [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) or [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) into the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field). See [<SG6>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sg6).

##### Load Zone

Load Zone \- A red or blue VEX IQ beam that is attached to the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) with VEX IQ pins. The [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone) is intended to receive [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) from a human Loader.

##### Matching Goal

Matching Goal \- A scoring bonus. See [<SC6>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc6).

##### Placed

Placed \- A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) status. See [<SC5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sc5).

##### Preload

Preload \- A [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) that is [Loaded](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#load) into a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) prior to a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). See [<SG5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sg5).

##### Scoring Object

Scoring Object \- A plastic object that can be added to a [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack). There are two types of [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) in VIQRC Mix & Match.

##### Pin

Pin \- An orange, blue, or red roughly cylindrical object with a diameter of approximately 3.15” (80mm), height of 4.5” (116mm), and a weight of approximately 2.5 ounces (71g).

##### Beam

Beam \- A gray, roughly rectangular object with a size of 9.88” (251mm) x 4.88” (124mm) x 1.97” (50mm) and a weight of approximately 6 ounces (170g).

##### Stack

Stack \- A set of two or more [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject).

##### Starting Pin

Starting Pin \- A [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) that begins the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) on a [Starting Pin Support](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpinsupport).

##### Starting Pin Support

Starting Pin Support \- One of four (4) red or blue structures, built out of VEX IQ parts, that is attached to the [Field Perimeter](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldperimeter). Each [Starting Pin Support](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpinsupport) holds a [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) of its color at the beginning of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), and until the [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) is removed by a Robot.

##### Event Partner

Event Partner \- The volunteer VEX IQ Robotics Competition tournament coordinator who serves as an overall manager for the volunteers, venue, event materials, and all other event considerations. [Event Partners](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) serve as the official liaison between the REC Foundation, the event volunteers, and event attendees.

##### Finals Match

Finals Match \- A [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) used to determine the [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) champions.

##### Head Referee

Head Referee \- A certified impartial volunteer responsible for enforcing the rules in this manual as written. [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) are the only people who may discuss ruling interpretations or scoring questions with Teams at an event. Large events (e.g., Signature Events, World Championships, etc.) might include multiple [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) at the [Event Partner’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) discretion.

##### Match Stop Time

Match Stop Time \- The time remaining (i.e., displayed on the timer or audience display) in a tiebreaker [Finals Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) (which only occurs for 1st place) when an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) ends the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) early by placing their controllers on the ground. The [Match Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchstoptime) is rounded down to the nearest even number. For example, if controllers are set down when the displayed time is 13 seconds, the [Match Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchstoptime) is recorded as 12 seconds. If an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) does not finish the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) early, they receive a default [Match Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchstoptime) of 0 seconds.

##### Practice Match

Practice Match \- A non-scored [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) used to provide time for Teams to get acquainted with the official playing [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field). [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) should not record or track standard gameplay [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) that occur during [Practice Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#practicematch). [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) that are egregious, unsportsmanlike and/or unsafe may be recorded and tracked at the discretion of the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee).

##### Qualification Match

Qualification Match \- A [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) used to determine the event rankings.

##### Robot Skills Challenge

Robot Skills Challenge \- A portion of the VEX IQ Robotics Competition. The [Robot Skills Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillschallenge) consists of [Driving Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) and [Autonomous Coding Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) as described in the General Definitions.

##### Scorekeeper Referee

Scorekeeper Referee \- An impartial volunteer responsible for tallying scores at the end of a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). [Scorekeeper Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scorekeeperreferee) do not make ruling interpretations, and should redirect any [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) questions regarding rules or scores to the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee).

##### Teamwork Challenge

Teamwork Challenge \- A portion of the VEX IQ Robotics Competition. The [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) consists of [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) and [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch), and may include [Practice Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#practicematch).

##### Driving Skills Match

Driving Skills Match \- A [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) consists of a sixty-second (one minute) [Driver Controlled Period](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivercontrolledperiod). There is no [Autonomous Period](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomousperiod). [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) can elect to end a [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) early as described in rule [<RSC8>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#rsc8) if they wish to record a [Skills Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime).

##### Autonomous Coding Skills Match

Autonomous Coding Skills Match \- An [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) consists of a sixty-second (one minute) [Autonomous Period](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomousperiod). There is no [Driver Controlled Period](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivercontrolledperiod). [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) can elect to end an [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) early if they wish to record a [Skills Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime).

##### Robot Skills Match

Robot Skills Match \- A [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) or [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch).

##### Skills Stop Time

Skills Stop Time \- The time remaining in a [Robot Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) when a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) ends the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) early.

1. If a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) does not end the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) early, they receive a default [Skills Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime) of 0.
2. The moment when the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) ends early is defined as the moment when the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) and [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) have come to a rest and the [Driver](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) has provided the agreed upon visual and audio signal to the Referee. See [<RSC8>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#rsc8) for more details.
3. If a Tournament Manager display is being used for field timing, then the [Skills Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime) is the time shown on the display when the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) is ended early (i.e., in 1-second increments).
4. If a manual timer is being used that counts down to 0 with greater accuracy than 1-second increments, then the time shown on the timer should be rounded up to the nearest second. For example, if the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is [Disabled](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disablement) and the timer shows 25.2 seconds, then the [Skills Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime) should be recorded as 26.

##### <SC1>

<SC1> All scoring statuses are evaluated after the Match ends, once all [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject), Field Elements, and [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) on the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) come to rest. See rule [<GG12>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg12) for more information and [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) details.

1. Referees should avoid contacting or moving [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) as much as possible while evaluating Scoring statuses. If an object must be moved to evaluate the status of another object, its status must be agreed upon by all [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) and the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee), and noted or recorded, before it is moved.
2. Referees should record counts based on verified scoring statuses evaluated after the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), using final positions of [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject), Field Elements, and [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). Points scored during a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) should not be deducted from a score, other than scoring which takes place after the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) due to continued [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) movement (see clause b of [<GG12>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg12)).

##### <SC2>

<SC2> All scoring statuses are evaluated visually by a Head Referee, to the best of their ability within the context of a given [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match)/event.

1. Referees and other event staff are not allowed to review any videos or pictures from the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). See [<T3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t3).
2. If there is a concern regarding the score of a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), only the [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) from that [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), not an [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult), may share their questions with the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee). See [<T3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t3).

##### <SC3>

<SC3>A Scoring Object can be Connected to another Scoring Object to form a [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack). To qualify as [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected), the resulting [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) must be roughly vertical (i.e., the [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) goes ‘up’ and not sideways) and cannot be in contact with a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).

1. [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) can be [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) in two ways: up from the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) or [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal), or up from a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam).
2. A [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) if it is fully nested (see Figure SC3-1) with another [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) and neither the [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) nor the resulting [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is touching a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).
3. A [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) if it is fully nested to one or more [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) and/or the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal) and is not touching a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).



2. A [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) cannot be [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to another [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam).
3. A [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) may be [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to up to three (3) [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) simultaneously if all [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) are fully nested with the [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam).
4. Each [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) that is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) directly to a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) is considered to be part of a separate [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack), and a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) may count as a color in up to three (3) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) simultaneously.
4. A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) that meets the requirements of the other clauses in this rule and is resting on one of the following Field Elements in a way that is more "up and down" than sideways should generally be considered as roughly vertical:




   - [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor)
   - [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone)
   - Any part of the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal)
   - The VEX IQ pieces that are attached to the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) around a [Square Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#squaregoal)
5. A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) that is leaning on / supported by a [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) that is not part of the [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) or a [Field Element](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldelements) other than those listed above should not be considered roughly vertical and should not count as [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) or a [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).
6. [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) contact with a lower [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) in a multi- [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) structure has no impact on the higher [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) in that structure for the purposes of clauses D & E. See <SE9> for an example.

Note: [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) cannot count as [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) or [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) in [Goals](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal) if they are not vertical. [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) that end the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) ‘knocked down’ or ‘tipped’ within the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), or that are not [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to other [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject), can only count toward the 2 points earned for a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) that ends the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) in contact with 2 or more [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject).

Note 2: A pair of [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) is considered fully nested if there’s no perceptable gap between the two objects, and neither object is being pushed away from the other by an external force or surface.

Significant Q&As:

- [Q&A 2664](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2664) \- Multiple scoring scenarios; Beam on floor generally leads to non-nested Pins
- [Q&A 2669](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2669) \- Scoring example with a Beam supported by the perimeter
- [Q&A 2679](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2679) \- A Beam can earn points if it’s Connected to the Standoff Goal with no Pins

##### <SC4>

<SC4> A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) that includes more than one color (blue, red, orange, or gray) of [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) receives additional points based on the number of colors in that [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack), up to three colors.

##### <SC5>

<SC5> A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is considered Placed in a Goal at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) if it meets all of the following criteria.

1. There are at least two (2) [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) in the [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).
2. No part of the [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is contacting a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).
3. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) meets one of the following criteria:




1. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is contacting the PET sheet and entirely within the center outline that defines the [Floor Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floorgoal) (maximum of four (4) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack)).
2. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is entirely within a [Square Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#squaregoal) (maximum of one (1) [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) per [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal)).
3. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is entirely within a < [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal) (maximum of three (3) [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) per [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal)).
4. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is above the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal) in one of the following configurations:




      - The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal)
      - The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) up from a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) that is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal)
      - The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) up from a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) that is part of another [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) that is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal)

##### <SC6>

<SC6> A [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) earns a Matching Goal bonus when one or more of the following criteria is met:

1. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is [Placed](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#placed) in a [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal) with a color that matches the bottom [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) in that [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack).
2. The [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) is [Connected](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#connected) to a [Beam](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam).

Each [Stack](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) can earn a maximum of one (1) [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) bonus.

Significant Q&As:

- [Q&A 2665](https://www.robotevents.com/VIQRC/2025-2026/QA/2665) \- One Pin connected to a Beam counts as a Stack

##### <SC7>

<SC7>A Starting Pin is Cleared if no part of its Starting Pin Support is within the volume of a [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

##### <SC8>

<SC8> A [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) will receive 2 points for ending the Match in contact with Scoring Objects in the following scenarios:

1. The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is directly contacting two or more [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject).
2. The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is directly contacting a [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) that is fully nested with one or more additional [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject).

##### <S1>

<S1>Stay safe, don’t damage the Field. If, at any time, the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) operation or [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) actions are deemed unsafe or have damaged any Field Elements or [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject), the offending [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may be [Disabled](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disablement) and/or [Disqualified](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) at the [Head Referee’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) discretion. The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) will require re-inspection before it may again take the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field).

Note: [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may not step onto the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) at any time. If a [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) requires stepping onto the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) during pre- [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) setup, this will be considered a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [<S1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#s1), [<GG3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg3), and/or [<SG1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sg1). The [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) may be removed from the current [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) at the [Head Referee’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) discretion.

Violation Notes: [Major Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation) should be reported to and/or discussed with the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) during the event, and should be reported to the REC Foundation Rules and Conduct Committee following the event.

##### <S2>

<S2>Students must be accompanied by an Adult. No [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) may attend a VEX IQ Robotics Competition event without a responsible [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) supervising them. The [Adult](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) must obey all rules and be careful to not violate [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student)-centered policies, but must be present for the full duration of the event in the case of an emergency. [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule may result in removal from the event.

Violation Notes: [<S2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#s2) [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) should be reported to the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) during the event, and should be reported to the REC Foundation Rules and Conduct Committee following the event.

##### <S3>

<S3>Each Student Team member must have a completed participant release form on file for the event and season. A [Student](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) member cannot participate in an event without a completed release form on file.

##### <G1>

<G1>Treat everyone with respect. All [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are expected to conduct themselves in a respectful and professional manner while competing in VEX IQ Robotics Competition events. If a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) or any of its members ( [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) or any [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) associated with the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team)) are disrespectful or uncivil to event staff, volunteers, or fellow competitors, they may be [Disqualified](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) from a current or upcoming [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) conduct pertaining to [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) may also impact a [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) eligibility for judged awards. Repeated or extreme [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) could result in a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) being [Disqualified](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) from an entire event, depending on the severity of the situation.

This rule exists alongside the REC Foundation Code of Conduct. [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of the Code of Conduct can be considered a [Major Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation) of [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) and can result in [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) from a current [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), an upcoming [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), an entire event, or (in extreme cases) an entire competition season. The Code of Conduct can be found [here](https://viqrc-kb.recf.org/hc/en-us/articles/9778593540247-Code-of-Conduct).

- Event attendees are not allowed to record audio or video of [Teams’](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) discussions with [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) or other event staff/volunteers.

More information regarding the event Code of Conduct process can be found at the [RECF Library](https://viqrc-kb.recf.org/hc/en-us/articles/16943810308503-Event-Code-of-Conduct-Process).

We all can contribute to creating a fun and inclusive event experience for all event attendees. Some examples include:

When dealing with difficult and stressful situations, it is…

- Okay for [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to be gracious and supportive when your [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) partner makes a mistake.
- Not okay for [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to harass, tease, or be disrespectful to your [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) partner when a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) does not go your way.

When a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) does not understand a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) ruling or score, it is…

- Okay for [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) to consult with a [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) to discuss a ruling per the process outlined in [<T3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t3) in a calm and respectful manner.
- Not okay for [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) to continue arguing with the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) after a decision has been finalized, or for [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to approach a [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) with ruling/scoring concerns.

When [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are getting ready for an upcoming [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), it is…

- Okay for [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) in an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) to develop a game strategy that utilizes the strengths of both [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) to cooperatively solve the game.
- Not okay for one [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) in an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) to ask another [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to sit in a corner during the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) or to intentionally play beneath their abilities.

Violation Notes: Any [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) may be considered a [Major Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation) and should be addressed on a case-by-case basis. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) at risk of a [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) [Major Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation) due to multiple disrespectful or uncivil behaviors will usually receive a “final warning”, although the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) is not required to provide one. All [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) [Major Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#majorviolation)/ [Disqualifications](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) should be reported to and/or discussed with the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) during the event, and should be reported to the REC Foundation Rules and Conduct Committee following the event.

##### <G2>

<G2>VIQRC is a student-centered program.
