This includes using different [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) for [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch), [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch), and/or [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch).
4. Multiple [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may not use the same [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). Once a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) has competed under a given [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) number at an event, it is “their” [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot); no other [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may EVER compete with it.

The intent of <R1a>, <R1b>, and <R1c> is to ensure an unambiguous level playing field for all [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team). [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are welcome (and encouraged) to improve or modify their [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) between events, or to collaborate with other [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to develop the best possible game solution.

However, a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) who brings and/or competes with two separate [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) at the same tournament has diminished the efforts of a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) who spent extra design time making sure that their one [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) can accomplish all of the game’s tasks. A multi- [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) organization that shares a single [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) has diminished the efforts of a multi- [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) organization that puts in the time, effort, and resources to undergo separate individual design processes and develop their own [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).

To help determine whether a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is a “separate [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot)” or not, use the Subsystem definitions found in [<R1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#r1). Above that, use common sense as referenced in [<G3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g3). If you can place two complete and legal [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) on a table next to each other, then they are two separate [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). Trying to decide if changing a pin, a wheel, or a motor constitutes a separate [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is missing the intent and spirit of this rule.

##### <R2>

<R2>Robots must represent the Team’s skill level. The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) must be designed, built, and programmed by members of the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team). [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) are permitted to mentor and teach design, building, and programming skills to the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) on the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), but may not design, build, or program that [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). See rules [<G2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g2), [<G4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g4), and [<G5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g5).

In VIQRC, we expect [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) to teach fundamental [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) principles like linkages, drivetrains, and manipulators, then allow the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) to determine which designs to implement and build on their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).

Similarly, [Adults](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#adult) are encouraged to teach the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) how to code various functions involving applicable sensors and mechanisms, then have the [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) program the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) from what they have learned.

##### <R3>

<R3>Robots must pass inspection. The [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) must pass inspection before being allowed to participate in any [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). Noncompliance with any [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) design or construction rule will result in removal from [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) or [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) of the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) at an event until the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is brought back into compliance, as described in the following subclauses.

1. Significant changes to a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), such as a partial or full swap of Subsystem 3, must be re-inspected before the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) may compete again.
2. All possible functional [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) configurations must be inspected before being used in competition.
3. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may be asked to submit to spot inspections by [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee). Refusal to submit will result in [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification).
4. If a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is determined to not be legal before a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) begins and cannot be brought into compliance before the scheduled [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) start time, the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) will be removed from the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field). The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) may remain at the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) so that the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) does not get assessed a “no-show” (per [<GG2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg2)).
5. [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) which have not passed inspection (i.e., that are in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of one or more [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) rules) will not be permitted to play in any [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) until they have done so. [<GG3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg3) will apply to any [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) that occur until the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) has passed inspection.
6. If a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) has passed inspection, but is later found to be in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) rule during or immediately following a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), then they will be [Disqualified](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) from that [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) and <R3d>/ [<GG3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg3) will apply until the [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) is remedied and the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is re-inspected. This is the only [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) that will be affected; any prior [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) that have already been completed will not be revisited. <R3d> will apply until the [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) is remedied and the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is re-inspected.
7. All inspection rules are to be enforced at the discretion of the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) within a given event. [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) legality at one event does not automatically imply legality at future events. [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) which rely on “edge-case” interpretations of subjective rules, such as whether a decoration is “non-functional” or not, should expect additional scrutiny during inspection.
8. Event staff and volunteers are allowed to photograph [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) during inspection and/or at other times as needed.

##### <R4>

<R4>There is a difference between accidentally and willfully violating a Robot rule. Any [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) rules, accidental or intentional, will result in a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) being unable to play until they pass inspection (per <R3d>).

However, [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) who intentionally and/or knowingly circumvent or violate rules to gain an advantage over their fellow competitors are in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of the spirit and ethos of the competition. Any [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this sort should be considered a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) and/or the REC Foundation Code of Conduct.

A [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) that circumvents a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) rule for a competitive advantage should receive an immediate [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) for the current [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) and be reported to the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) for discussion with the REC Foundation Regional Support Manager. As a result of that discussion, the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may be [Disqualified](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) from the event. The [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) should also be reported to the REC Foundation Rules and Conduct Committee following the event.

##### <R5>

<R5>Robots must fit within an 11” x 20” x 15” (279.4mm x 508mm x 381.0mm) volume.

1. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) using more than one possible [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) configuration at the beginning of [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) must tell the inspector(s) and have the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) inspected in all configurations. Rule <R3c> will apply if a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is placed in an uninspected configuration (i.e., will not be permitted to play until re-inspected, but will not be considered a “no-show”).
2. A [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may NOT have its [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) inspected in one configuration and then place it in an uninspected configuration at the start of a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

##### <R6>

<R6>Officially registered Team numbers must be displayed on Robot License Plates. To participate in an official VEX IQ Robotics Competition Event, a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) must first register on RobotEvents.com and receive a VEX IQ Robotics Competition [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) number.

This [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) number must be legibly displayed on exactly two (2) VEX IQ Robotics Competition [License Plates](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#licenseplate) on opposing sides of the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may use the official VEX IQ Robotics Competition License Plate (VEX Part Number 228-7401) or a plain paper version of matching size, such as [this template in the REC Library](https://viqrc-kb.recf.org/hc/en-us/articles/28277975906199-Printable-VEX-IQ-Robotics-Competition-License-Plate).

1. [License Plates](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#licenseplate) are considered functional components, and must meet the requirements of all [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) rules.
2. [License Plates](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#licenseplate) must be clearly visible at all times. For example, [License Plates](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#licenseplate) must not be in a position that would be easily obstructed by a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) mechanism during standard [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) play.
3. Additional [License Plates](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#licenseplate) cannot be used on the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) for any purpose.

##### <R7>

<R7>Let it go after the Match is over. [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) must be designed to permit easy removal of [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) from their [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) without requiring that the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) have power or remote control after the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) is over.

##### <R8>

<R8>Robots have one Brain. [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) are limited to one (1) VEX IQ Robot Brain. Any other microcontrollers or processing devices are not allowed, even as non-functional decorations.

This includes microcontrollers that are part of other VEX product lines, such as VEX Cortex, VEX EXP, VEXpro, VEX CTE, VEX RCR, VEX V5, VEX GO, or VEX Robotics by HEXBUG\*. This also includes devices that are unrelated to VEX, such as Raspberry Pi or Arduino devices.

1. If using a first generation VEX IQ Brain, [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) must use one (1) VEX IQ 900 MHz radio, VEX IQ 2.4 GHz radio, or VEX IQ Smart Radio in conjunction with their VEX IQ Robot Brain. The VEX IQ Brain and VEX IQ Controller may not be physically connected during a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), and may only communicate through the radio.
2. Additional Robot Brains cannot be used on the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) (even Robot Brains that are not connected).

##### <R9>

<R9>Keep the power button accessible. The on/off button on the VEX IQ Robot Brain must be accessible without moving or lifting the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). All screens and/or lights must also be easily visible by competition personnel to assist in diagnosing [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) problems.

This rule is in place to ensure the safety of both competitors and field staff. In the event that a [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) needs to be quickly powered off—whether due to a malfunction, entanglement, or other safety concern—it is crucial that the power button remains easily accessible. This allows competitors and/or field personnel to safely [Disable](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disablement) the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) without putting their hands near moving parts or other hazards inside the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). Additionally, keeping screens and indicator lights visible helps officials diagnose issues efficiently, minimizing downtime and ensuring a smooth competition experience.

##### <R10>

<R10>Firmware. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) must use VEXos version 2.2.1 or newer on Gen1 Brains, or VEXos version 1.0.8 or newer on Gen2 Brains. The latest firmware can be found at [https://link.vex.com/firmware](https://link.vex.com/firmware). Custom firmware modifications are not permitted.

1. The minimum version requirement is subject to change over the course of the season.
2. When the minimum version is updated, [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) have a two week (14 calendar day) grace period from the time the minimum version is changed to update their firmware to the latest minimum version.
3. VEX Robotics reserves the right to deem any firmware update critical, and remove the allowable grace period.

##### <R11>

<R11>Motors. [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) may use up to six (6) VEX IQ Smart Motors.

1. Additional motors cannot be used on the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) (even motors that aren’t connected).

##### <R12>

<R12>Batteries. The only allowable sources of electrical power for a VEX IQ Robotics Competition [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) are one (1) VEX IQ Robot Battery (first or second generation) or six (6) AA batteries via the Robot AA Battery Holder (228-3493).

1. Additional batteries cannot be used on the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) (even batteries that aren’t connected).
2. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are permitted to have an external power source (such as a rechargeable battery pack) plugged into their VEX IQ Controller during a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), provided that this power source is connected safely and does not violate any other rules (such as [<GG1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg1)).

Note: Although it is legal, the Robot AA Battery Holder (228-3493) is not recommended for use in the VEX IQ Robotics Competition.

##### <R13>

<R13>One Controller per Robot. No more than one (1) VEX IQ Controller may control a single [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).

1. No physical or electrical modification of the Controller is allowed under any circumstances.




1. Attachments which assist the [Drivers](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) in holding or manipulating buttons/joysticks on the IQ Controller (including 3D-printed controller attachments) are permitted, provided that they do not involve direct physical or electrical modification of the Controller itself.
2. No other methods of controlling the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) (light, sound, etc.) are permissible.




1. Using sensor feedback to augment [Driver](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) control (such as motor encoders or the Vision Sensor) is permitted.
2. See [<RSC5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#rsc5), [<RSC6>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#rsc6), and [<RSC7>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#rsc7) for more information about operating the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) during [Autonomous Coding Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch).

##### <R14>

<R14>Robots are built from the VEX IQ product line. [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) may be built ONLY from official [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) components from the VEX IQ product line, unless otherwise specifically noted within these rules.

1. Official VEX IQ products are ONLY available from VEX Robotics. To determine whether or not a product is “official” and legal for competition use, consult the following sources:




1. [VEX IQ Robotics Competition Legal Parts Appendix](https://link.vex.com/docs/viqc/legal-parts)
2. [VEX IQ Robotics Competition Illegal Parts Appendix](https://link.vex.com/docs/viqc/illegal-parts)
3. [www.vexiq.com](http://www.vexiq.com/)
2. If an inspector or [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) questions whether something is an official VEX IQ component, the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) will be required to provide documentation that proves the component’s source. Such documentation may include receipts, part numbers, or other printed documentation.
3. Only VEX IQ components specifically designed for use in [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) construction are allowed. Using additional components outside their typical purpose is against the intent of the rule (i.e., please don’t try using VEX IQ apparel, [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) or event support materials, packaging, Field Elements, or other non- [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) products on a VEX IQ Robotics Competition [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot)).
4. Official Robotics components from the VEX IQ product line that have been discontinued are still legal for [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) use. However, [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) must be aware of <R14b>.
5. Additional VEX IQ products that are released during the season are legal for use, unless otherwise noted on their product pages.
6. VEX IQ Smart Cables may only be used for connecting legal electronic devices to the VEX IQ Robot Brain.


Note: A comprehensive list of legal VEX IQ parts can be found in the VEX IQ Robotics Competition Legal Parts Appendix, at [https://www.vexrobotics.com/iq/competition/viqrc-current-game](https://www.vexrobotics.com/iq/competition/viqc-current-game). This Appendix is updated as needed if/when new VEX IQ parts are released, and may not coincide with scheduled Game Manual updates.

##### <R15>

<R15>Prohibited items. The following types of mechanisms and components are NOT allowed:

1. Those that could potentially damage Field Elements or [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject).
2. Those that could potentially damage or entangle other [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot).
3. Grease, oil, graphite, and/or any other lubricant or plastic additive.
4. Tape and/or any other material that adheres to or changes a legal part, other than non-functional decorations as permitted by [<R17>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#r17).
5. Products from the VEX 123, VEX V5, VEX CTE, VEX EXP, Cortex, or VEXpro product lines, unless specifically allowed by a clause of [<R16>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#r16).
6. Electrical components from the VEX Robotics by HEXBUG\* product line.
7. Electrical components from the VEX GO product line.
8. 3D printed parts for any purpose, including non-functional decorations.
9. Additional illegal parts are listed in the VEX IQ Robotics Competition Illegal Parts Appendix, at [https://link.vex.com/ docs/viqrc/illegal-parts](https://link.vex.com/%20docs/viqrc/illegal-parts). This Appendix is updated as needed, and may not coincide with scheduled Game Manual updates.

##### <R16>

<R16>Legal Non-VEX IQ components. [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) are allowed to use the following additional “non-VEX IQ” components:

1. Rubber bands that are identical in length and thickness to those included in the VEX IQ product line (#32, #64, #117B, & #170).
2. ⅛” metal shafts from the VEX V5 product line.
3. Other products from the VEX V5 product line that are also cross-listed as part of the VEX IQ product line are legal. A “cross-listed” product is one which can be found in both the VEX IQ and VEX V5 sections of the VEX Robotics website.
4. Mechanical/structural components from the VEX Robotics by HEXBUG\* product line are legal for [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) construction.
5. Mechanical/structural components from the VEX GO product line are legal for [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) construction.
6. Aerosol-based cooling/freeze spray may be used to assist in cooling motors. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) using freeze spray or similar products in ways that may reasonably be deemed unsafe could be subject to [<S1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#s1) [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation).
7. Cleaners, disinfectants, and/or sanitizers may be used to assist in cleaning [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), parts, components, etc. VEX Robotics recommends [these procedures](https://kb.vex.com/hc/en-us/articles/360047126751-VEX-Product-Disinfecting-Guide) for cleaning/disinfecting/sanitizing [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) parts.

##### <R17>

<R17>Decorations are allowed. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may add non-functional decorations, provided that they do not affect [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) performance in any significant way or affect the outcome of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). These decorations must be in the spirit of the competition. Inspectors and [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) will have final say in what is considered “non-functional.” Unless otherwise specified below, non-functional decorations are governed by all standard [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) rules.

1. Decorations must be in the spirit of an educational competition.
2. To be considered “non-functional,” any decorations must be backed by legal materials that provide the same functionality. For example, a giant decal cannot be used to prevent [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) from falling out of the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) unless it is backed by VEX IQ material. A simple way to check this is to determine if removing the decoration would impact the performance of the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) in any way.
**\\* The HEXBUG brand is a registered trademark belonging to Spin Master Corp** 4. The use of non-toxic paint is considered a legal non-functional decoration. However, any paint being used as an adhesive or to impact how tightly parts fit together would be classified as functional.

[Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) should be mindful of any non-functional decorations which could risk “distracting” an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) partner [Robot’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) Vision Sensor or other sensors.

##### <R18>

<R18>Pneumatics. [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) using parts from the VEX IQ Pneumatics Kit (228-8795) must satisfy all of the following criteria:

1. No more than two (2) Air Tanks, including any that aren’t connected.
2. No more than (1) Air Pump, including any that aren’t connected.
3. No additional parts that are not included in the VEX IQ Pneumatics Kit (e.g., unofficial tubing or fittings).


There is no limit on the number of Pneumatic Cylinders or Pneumatic Solenoids that may be used, provided that no other rules are violated. There are no restrictions on running the Air Pump prior to (or during) [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

The intent of <R18a> is to limit [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) to the air pressure stored in two Air Tanks, as well as the normal working air pressure contained in any Pneumatic Cylinders and tubing on the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot). [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may not use other elements for the purposes of storing or generating air pressure.

Using Pneumatic Cylinders or additional tubing solely for additional air storage is in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of the spirit of this rule. Similarly, using Pneumatic Cylinders and/or tubing without an actual pneumatic system (e.g., Air Tanks and/or a Air Pump) is also in [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of the spirit of this rule.

##### <R19>

<R19>Modifications of parts. Parts may NOT be modified unless specifically listed as an exception in this rule. Examples of illegal modifications include, but are not limited to, bending, cutting, sanding, gluing, lubricating, taping, and melting. The following exceptions are the only legal modifications of parts:

1. Cutting metal VEX IQ or VEX V5 shafts to custom lengths.
2. Bending parts which are intended to be flexible, such as string, rubber bands, or thin plastic sheets.
3. Cutting VEX IQ pneumatic tubing to custom lengths.
4. Tying knots to shorten or connect string or rubber bands.

##### <T1>

<T1>Head Referees have ultimate and final authority on all gameplay and robot ruling decisions during the competition.

1. [Scorekeeper Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scorekeeperreferee) score the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), and may serve as observers or advisers for the [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee), but may not determine any [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) directly.
2. When issuing a [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification) or [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) to a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) should attempt to notify the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) as the [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) occurs, and after the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) must provide the rule number of the specific rule that has been Violated and record the [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) in the Match Anomaly Log.
3. [CoC-related Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) require additional escalation beyond the [Head Referee’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) initial ruling, including (but not limited to) investigation by RECF representatives.
4. [Event Partners](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) may not overrule a [Head Referee’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) gameplay or [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) decisions.
5. Every [Qualification Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) and [Finals Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) must be watched by a certified [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee). [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) may only watch one [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) at a time; if multiple [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) are happening simultaneously on separate [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), each [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) must have its own [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee). [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) must follow the rules in this game manual and the Q&A, and must make rulings consistent with the intent of the game manual and Q&A.
6. At a minimum, every [Robot Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) must be watched by a trained [Scorekeeper Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scorekeeperreferee), who may only watch one [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) at a time. If multiple [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) are happening simultaneously on separate [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), each [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) must have its own [Scorekeeper Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scorekeeperreferee). A certified [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) must be available at the event to explain a rule, [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification), [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation), or other penalty to [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) in [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) as needed in support of the [Scorekeeper Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scorekeeperreferee) at skills [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field).

Note from the VEX GDC: The rules contained in this Game Manual are written to be enforced by human [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee). Many rules have “black-and-white” criteria that can be easily checked. However, some rulings will rely on a judgment call from this human [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee). In these cases, [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) will make their calls based on what they and the [Scorekeeper Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scorekeeperreferee) saw, what guidance is provided by their official support materials (the Game Manual and the Q&A), and most crucially, the context of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) in question.

The VEX IQ Robotics Competition does not have video replay, our [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) do not have absolute sensors to count scores, and most events do not have the resources for an extensive review conference between each [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

When an ambiguous rule results in a controversial call, there is a natural instinct to wonder what the “right” ruling “should have been,” or what the GDC “would have ruled.” This is ultimately an irrelevant question; our answer is that when a rule specifies “ [Head Referee’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) discretion” (or similar), then the “right” call is the one made by the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) in the moment. The VEX GDC designs games, and writes rules, with this expectation (constraint) in mind.

##### <T2>

<T2>Head Referees must be qualified. VEX IQ [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) must have all of the following qualifications:

1. Be at least 16 years of age.
2. Be approved by the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner).
3. Be an REC Foundation Certified VIQRC [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) for the current season. Visit [the REC Library](https://kb.roboticseducation.org/hc/en-us/articles/14527449656087-REC-Foundation-Volunteer-Certifications) for more details.
4. Cannot be the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) or a Judge Advisor for the event.

Note: [Scorekeeper Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scorekeeperreferee) must be at least 15 years of age, and must be approved by the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner).

##### <T3>

<T3>The Drive Team Members are permitted to immediately appeal the Head Referee’s ruling. If [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) wish to dispute a score or ruling, they must stay in the [Driver Station](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driverstation) until the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) talks with them. The [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) may choose to meet with the [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) at another location and/or at a later time so that the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) has time to reference materials or resources to help with the decision. Once the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) announces that their decision has been made final, the issue is over and no more appeals may be made (see rule [<T1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t1)).

1. Referees are not permitted to review any photo or video [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) recordings when determining a score or ruling.
2. [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) are the only individuals permitted to explain a rule, [Disqualification](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#disqualification), or [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) to the Teams in a [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). Teams should never consult other field personnel, including [Scorekeeper Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scorekeeperreferee), regarding a ruling clarification.

Communication and conflict resolution skills are an important life skill for [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) to practice and learn. In VEX IQ Robotics Competitions, we expect [Students](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#student) to practice proper conflict resolution using the proper chain of command. [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of this rule may be considered a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) and/or the Code of Conduct.

Some events may choose to utilize a “question box” or other designated location for discussions with [Head Referees](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee). Offering a “question box” is within the discretion of the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) and/or [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee), and may act as an alternate option for asking [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) to remain in the [Driver Station](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driverstation) (although all other aspects of this rule apply).

However, by using this alternate location, [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) acknowledge that they are forfeiting the opportunity to use any contextual information involving the specific state of the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) at the end of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). For example, it is impossible to appeal whether a game element was scored or not if the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) has already been reset. If this information is pertinent to the appeal, [Drive Team Members](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driveteammembers) should still remain in the [Driver Station](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driverstation), and relocate to the “question box” once the [Head Referee](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#headreferee) has been made aware of the concern and/or any relevant context.

##### <T4>

<T4>The Event Partner has ultimate authority regarding all non-gameplay decisions during an event. The Game Manual is intended to provide a set of rules for successfully playing VIQRC Mix & Match; it is not intended to be an exhaustive compilation of guidelines for running a VEX IQ Robotics Competition event. Rules such as, but not limited to, the following examples are at the discretion of the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) and should be treated with the same respect as the Game Manual:

- Venue access
- Pit spaces
- Health and safety
- [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) registration and/or competition eligibility
- [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) conduct away from competition [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field)

This rule exists alongside [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1), [<S1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#s1), and [<G3>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g3). Even though there isn’t a rule that says “do not steal from the concession stand,” it would still be within an [Event Partner’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) authority to remove a thief from the competition.

##### <T5>

<T5>Be prepared for minor field variance. [Field Element](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldelements) tolerances and [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) positions may vary from nominal by up to ±0.5” \[12.7mm\], unless otherwise specified. The rotation of [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) is not specified. If a [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) is within tolerance, either on the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) or on a [Starting Pin Support](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#startingpinsupport), it should not be adjusted before the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match). [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are encouraged to design their [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) accordingly. Please make sure to check Appendix A for more specific nominal dimensions and tolerances.

The [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) and Field Elements are designed to be assembled and disassembled multiple times each year. [Event Partners](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) store and transport [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) between events, and the individuals setting up the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) at one event may differ from those at the next. While every effort will be made to ensure minimal variance, Teams should expect that any [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) may be slightly different than another, and prepare accordingly. Just because something works on one [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) does not fully guarantee it will work on the next, and is not enough evidence alone to determine if a [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) is out of tolerance.

##### <T6>

<T6>Fields and Field Elements may be repaired at the Event Partner’s discretion. All competition [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) and other Field Elements at an event must be set up in accordance with the specifications in Appendix A and/or other applicable support materials. Minor aesthetic customizations or repairs are permitted, provided that they do not impact gameplay (see [<T4>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t4)).

Examples of permissible modifications include, but are not limited to:

1. Replacing a damaged or missing VEX IQ component with an identical part of any color.
2. Elevating the playing [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) off of the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) (common heights are 10” to 24” \[254mm to 609.6mm\]).
3. Using off-the-shelf PVC to replace a damaged or missing pipe.
4. Using double-side tape to stick the edges of the templates to the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) in cases where the sheet pins don't adequately secure the [Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#goal) templates; cannot be requested by [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) if the sheets pins are sufficient to secure the templates to the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field)
5. Using (or not using) the included VEX IQ sheet attachment pins to mark object locations for field reset.

##### <T7>

<T7>Fields at an event must be consistent with each other. There are many types of permissible aesthetic and/or logistical modifications that may be made to competition [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) at the [Event Partner’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) discretion. If an event has multiple [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), they must all incorporate the same permissible/applicable modifications. If an event has multiple Robot Skills Challenge Fields, they must all incorporate the same permissible/applicable modifications. For example, if one Teamwork Challenge [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) is elevated, then all [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) must be elevated to the same height.

Examples of these modifications may include, but are not limited to:

- Elevating the playing [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) off of the [Floor](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#floor) (common heights are 12” to 24” \[30.5cm to 61cm\])
- Field display monitors
- [Field Perimeter](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#fieldperimeter) decorations (e.g., LED lights, sponsor banners attached to risers)

- Using (or not using) the included VEX IQ sheet attachment pins to mark object locations for field reset.

Note: If an event has dedicated [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) for [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch), there is no requirement for them to have the same consistent modifications as the [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field). See [<T16>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t16) for more details.

##### <T8>

<T8>Qualification Matches will occur according to the official match schedule. This schedule will indicate [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) partners, [Qualification Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) times, and, if the event has multiple [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field), which [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) each [Qualification Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) will be played on.

1. [Practice Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#practicematch) may be included in the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) schedule at some events, but are not required. If [Practice Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#practicematch) are run, every effort will be made to equalize practice time for all Teams.
2. A [Qualification Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) can only start before its scheduled time if all Teams, [Robots](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot), and assigned volunteers are at the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) and ready to play.
3. Any multi-division event must be approved by the REC Foundation RSM prior to the event, and divisions must be assigned in sequential order by [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) number.

Note: The official [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) schedule is subject to changes at the [Event Partner’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) discretion.

##### <T9>

<T9> Each Team will be scheduled Qualification Matches as follows.

1. When in a tournament, the tournament must have a minimum of six (6) [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) per [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) at local qualifying events and eight (8) for a Championship event.
2. When in a league, there must be at least three (3) league ranking sessions, with at least one (1) week between sessions. Each session must have a minimum of two (2) [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) per [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team). The suggested number of [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) per [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) for a standard league ranking session is four (4). [Event Partners](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) may choose to have [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) as part of their league finals session.

##### <T10>

<T10> Teams are ranked by their average Qualification Match scores.

1. When in a tournament, every [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) will be ranked based on the same number of [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch).




1. For tournaments that have more than one (1) division, Teams will be ranked among all Teams in their specific division. Each division will have its own set of [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch). The winners of each division will then have an overall event Finals. Any multi-division event must be approved by the REC Foundation Regional Support Manager prior to the event, and divisions must be assigned in sequential order by [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) number.
2. When in a league, every [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) will be ranked based on the number of [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) played. Teams that participate in less than 60% of the total [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) available will be ranked below Teams that participate in at least 60% of the total [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) available (e.g., if the league offers 3 ranking sessions with 4 [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) per [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team), Teams that participate in 8 or more [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) will be ranked higher than Teams who participate in 7 or fewer [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match)). Being a no-show to a [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) that a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) is scheduled in still constitutes participation for these calculations.
3. A certain number of a [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) lowest [Qualification Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) scores will be excluded from the rankings based on the quantity of [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) each [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) plays. Excluded scores do not affect participation for leagues. “No show” [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), as described in [<GG2>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg2), are not considered lowest scores for the purposes of calculating a [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) [Qualification Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) ranking and will never be excluded from the calculation.

4. In some cases, a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) will be asked to play an additional [Qualification Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch). The extra [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) will be identified on the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) schedule with an asterisk and will not impact the [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) ranking (or participation for leagues). Teams are reminded that [<G1>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#g1) is always in effect and Teams are expected to behave as if the additional [Qualification Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) counted.

##### <T11>

<T11>Qualification Match tiebreakers. [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) rankings are determined throughout [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) by:

1. Removing the [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) lowest score and comparing the new average score.
2. Removing the [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) next lowest score and comparing the new average score (on through all scores).
3. If the Teams are still tied, the Teams will be sorted by random electronic draw.

##### <T12>

<T12>How Alliances are formed for Teamwork Matches. During each [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), two (2) Teams form an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) that will play on the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field).

1. [Qualification Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) [Alliances](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) are randomly assigned by the tournament software.
2. [Finals Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) [Alliances](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) are assigned as follows based on Teams’ rankings after all [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) have concluded (see [<T10>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t10)):




1. The first- and second-ranked Teams form an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance).
2. The third- and fourth-ranked Teams form an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance).
3. And so on, until all Teams participating in [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) have formed an [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance).

##### <T13>

<T13>Teams playing in Finals Matches. The number of [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch), and therefore the number of Teams who will participate in [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch), is determined by the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner). Events that qualify teams directly to the VEX Robotics World Championship must have a minimum of five (5) [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) if there are ten (10) or more Teams in attendance.

##### <T14>

<T14>Finals Match Schedule. [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) are played sequentially, starting with the lowest-ranked [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance). Each [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) will participate in one (1) [Finals Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch). The [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) with the highest [Finals Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) score is the [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) champion.

1. [Alliances](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) are ranked by their [Finals Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) score. The highest-scoring [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) is in first place, the second-highest-scoring [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) is in second place, etc.
2. Ties for first place will result in a series of tiebreaker [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch), starting with the lower-seeded [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance). The [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) with the highest tiebreaker [Finals Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) score will be declared the [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) champion.




1. If the tiebreaker [Finals Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) scores are tied, the [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) with the higher [Match Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchstoptime) will be declared the winner.
2. If the [Match Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchstoptime) is also tied, a second series of tiebreaker [Finals Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) will be played. If this second series of tiebreaker [Finals Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch) is also tied, then the higher-seeded [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) will be declared the winner.
3. If there is a tie for a place other than first, the higher-seeded [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) will receive the higher rank.

Example 1: [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) 6 and [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) 3 are tied for first place. During the tiebreaker [Finals Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#finalsmatch), [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) 6 scores 13 points and has a [Match Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchstoptime) of 12 seconds. [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) 3 scores 13 points and has a [Match Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchstoptime) of 10 seconds. [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) 6 is the [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) winner.

Example 2: [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) 4 and [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) 5 are tied for third place. [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) 4 is the third place winner and [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) 5 is the fourth place winner. In this way, the lower ranked [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) must “overcome” the higher ranked [Alliance](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#alliance) in order to become the [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) champion.

##### <T15>

<T15>Skills Match Schedule. Teams play [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) on a first-come, first-served basis. Each [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) will get the opportunity to play exactly three (3) [Driving Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) and three (3) [Autonomous Coding Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) at each tournament and/or League Session.

Teams should review the event agenda and their [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) schedule to determine when the best possible time is to complete their [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch). If the [Robot Skills Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillschallenge) area closes before a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) has completed all six (6) [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch), but it is determined that there was adequate time given, then the [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) will automatically forfeit those unused [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).

Details regarding logistics of Skills-Only Events can be found in the [REC Foundation Qualifying Criteria](https://kb.roboticseducation.org/hc/en-us/articles/5474199602071-Qualifying-Criteria-for-VIQRC-VRC-and-VEX-U-Events) document.

1. [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) are only available to [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) who participate in [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch), unless the event is an approved Skills-Only Event. [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) who participate in [Qualification Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#qualificationmatch) during a specific League Ranking Session are the only [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) who can participate in [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) at that session.
2. Skills scores recorded by ineligible [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) will be deleted from Tournament Manager before the event is finalized on RobotEvents.com.

##### <T16>

<T16>There is no requirement that Skills Challenge fields have the same consistent modifications as the Teamwork fields. For example, there is no requirement that [Robot Skills Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillschallenge) [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) are elevated to the same height as [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field).

In order to use non-conforming [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) for [Robot Skills Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillschallenge) [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) (e.g. during lunch), the following steps should be taken:

- Teams must be informed that the [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) may have some differences from the [Robot Skills Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillschallenge) [Fields](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) (e.g., they might be elevated).
- Teams must be given an opportunity to select which type of [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) they want to use, i.e. they cannot be required to use a [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) for any [Robot Skills Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillschallenge) [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).


##### <T17>

<T17> Skills Rankings at events. Teams will be ranked at an event based on the following scores and tiebreakers:

01. Sum of highest [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) score and highest [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) Score.
02. Highest [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) score.
03. Second-highest [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) score.
04. Second-highest [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) score.
05. Highest sum of [Skills Stop Times](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime) from a [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) highest [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) and highest [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) (i.e., the [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) in point 1).
06. Highest [Skills Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime) from a [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) highest [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) (i.e., the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) in point 2).
07. Third-highest [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) score
08. Third-highest [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) score.
09. If the tie cannot be broken after all above criteria (i.e., both Teams have the exact same scores and [Skills Stop Times](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime) for each [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) and [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch)), then the following ordered criteria will be used to determine which [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) had the “best” [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch):




    1. Points for [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack) in the [Standoff Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#standoffgoal)
    2. Points from [Matching Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#matchinggoal) Bonus
    3. Points for 2-color and 3-color [Stacks](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#stack)
10. If the tie still cannot be broken, the same process in the step above will be applied to the Teams’ highest [Driving Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch).
11. If the tie still isn’t broken, the [Event Partner](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#eventpartner) may choose to allow Teams to have one more deciding [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), or both Teams may be declared the winner.

##### <T18>

<T18> Skills Rankings globally. Teams are ranked based on their Robot Skills scores from Tournaments and Leagues that upload results to RobotEvents.com, according to the following tiebreakers.

1. Highest Robot Skills score (combined [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) and [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) Score from a single event).
2. Highest [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) score (from any event).
3. Highest sum of [Skills Stop Times](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime) from the [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) used for point 1.
4. Highest [Skills Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime) from the [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) used for point 2.
5. Highest [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) score (from any event).
6. Highest [Skills Stop Time](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#skillsstoptime) from the [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) score used in point 5.
7. Earliest posting of the highest [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) score.




1. The first [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to post a score ranks ahead of other Teams that post the same score at a later time, all else being equal.
8. Earliest posting of the highest [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) score.




1. The first [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) to post a score ranks ahead of other Teams that post the same score at a later time, all else being equal.

##### <T19>

<T19>Robot Skills at League Events. At league events in which Teams may submit [Robot Skills Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillschallenge) scores across multiple sessions, the Robot Skills scores (combined highest [Autonomous Coding Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch) and [Driving Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) scores) used for rankings will be calculated from [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) within the same session.

For example, consider the following scores for a hypothetical [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) across two league event sessions:

This [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) would have a Robot Skills score of 72 for this event’s rankings, and their scores from Session 2 would be used for the event and global tiebreakers listed in [<T17>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t17) and [<T18>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#t18).

##### <RSC1>

<RSC1>Standard rules apply in most cases. All rules from previous sections apply to the [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch), unless otherwise specified in this section.

Violation Notes:

- [Violations](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) of <GG>, <SG>, and <RSC> rules that occur during a [Robot Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) should only affect the outcome of that [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) and should not be considered when determining whether a [Violation](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#violation) has been repeated during the event.

##### <RSC2>

<RSC2>Scoring Robot Skills Matches. For each [Robot Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch), [Teams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) are awarded a score based on the standard scoring rules.

##### <RSC3>

<RSC3>Robot and Field setup for Skills Matches. The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) and [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) are set up the same as a [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) Match, with the following modifications:

1. The layout of [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) for a Mix & Match [Robot Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) differs from the layout for [Teamwork Challenge](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#teamworkchallenge) [Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match), as shown in Figure RSC3-1.




   - [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) and [Beams](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#beam) start in different locations on the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field).
   - The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) receives one red [Pin](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) as a Preload.
   - Six [Pins](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#pin) (two red, two blue, and two orange) begin the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) in the Red [Driver Station](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driverstation) for [Loading](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#load).
2. The blue [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone) is not used in [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch). [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) of any color may be introduced into the red [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone) only. This includes any [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) that is reintroduced after leaving the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) during the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).
3. The [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) must be placed in contact with the structure of the red [Triangle Goal](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#trianglegoal) at the beginning of the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match) and after the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) is reset under rule [<GG10>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#gg10) or [<RSC5>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#rsc5).

##### <RSC4>

<RSC4>Loader and Driver differences. All criteria listed in [<SG6>](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#sg6) apply as written (e.g., a Loader cannot put a [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) into a [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone) if there’s already a [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) there). [Loading](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#load) is modified as follows:

1. In both [Driving Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#drivingskillsmatch) and [Autonomous Coding Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#autonomouscodingskillsmatch), any [Driver](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#driver) who is not currently Driving the [Robot](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robot) may also serve as a Loader (i.e., a [Team](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) may have one, two, or three Loaders at any given time).
2. The blue [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone) is not used in [Robot Skills Matches](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch), and [Scoring Objects](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) may only be introduced into the red [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone). This includes any [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) that is reintroduced after leaving the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) during the [Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#match).
3. Any [Scoring Object](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#scoringobject) that leaves the [Field](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#field) during a [Robot Skills Match](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#robotskillsmatch) should be given to the [Team’s](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#team) human Loader for reintroduction at the red [Load Zone](https://www.vexrobotics.com/mix-and-match-manual#loadzone), regardless of that object’s color.
4.
